text:
I did my first loaf after reading all the reviews and my husband loves it. I'd like to suggest letting the loaf sit for 15 minutes before cutting, this will prevent oozing of the cheese. 
When I made it the second time, I dicovered a way to simplify the rolling process and had great success.
I divided my meat mixture into 3 batches and cheese into 2 batches (like a lasagne).  Fill the bottom of a 9x13 dish with the 1st batch, then sprinkle cheese on top, avoiding the edges.
I then pat the 2nd batch on top, taking a little care to seal the edges with a spatula.  Cheese on top of that.
Finally, the 3rd batch of meat on top of that, sealing the edges again.
I then sprinkled ketchup and mustard overall.  It came out tasting the same as the recipe indicated, but saves much time and effort.

text:
This is a great recipe!  I only gave it 4 stars because I found the "jelly-roll" effect to be more trouble than it was worth.  Instead, I just half the meat mixture and make a channel for the cheese down the center and then top with the remaining meat mixture. It is much more simple and it isn't as messy!  Tastes fantastic as is or is easy to jazz up too!

text:
Easy recipe to follow, traditional meatloaf with a fun twist.Here are some tips:

To prevent your meatloaf from breaking up at the bottom or being greasy, add 1 solid layer of foil at the bottom of the baking pan, then add another layer of foil on top of that, but poke small holes in the top layer. The grease from the beef drips through the holes and stays away from beef and the bottom foil catches it for easy clean up after cooking!

Also, to make the jelly roll effect easier, try flattening the beef onto a large piece of foil, add cheese, then lift the edges of the foil to manipulate the beef instead of your hands. I found this to be easier and less messy.

text:
The way I jelly-roll this is I take a baking sheet and line with wax paper a little longer than the pan and spread the meat mixture out the full length of the pan, its about 3/4 of the way up the sides, spread shredded cheddar cheese all the way around keeping an inch or two from the sides and end then pulling up on the wax paper I start to roll, roll a little pull the wax paper, keep it fairly tight, roll a little and pull the paper till the end. I spray a little cooking spray onto the pan turn the roll sideways and voila - fold the  ends down and form a good "seel" at the ends and bake. Be sure to let set for 10min or so so the cheese doesnt ooze all over. Enjoy - I like to top it with Ketchup the last 15min of cooking as well.

text:
I invested in a two part meatloaf pan and can't say enough about it.  I put my meat mixture in the top pan which fits inside the 2nd pan.  As the loaf cooks, all the fat runs out into the bottom pan.  I have never had a dry meatloaf, even when using low fat meats like ground turkey, but the fat is reduced. It is nonstick and cleans up like a dream. You could also use a diposable foil pan to hold the mixture and poke several holes in the bottom.  Set it in your regular meatloaf pan and the fat will drain out as above.

text:
this was very good...i used italian blend cheese for a filling with some garlic and tabasco in the meatloaf but otherwise followed the recipe...keep the meat mixture at least 2 inches thick when you spread it out on the foil before rolling (don't use waxed paper...it gets wet...and spray the foil first with oil)...don't try and spread it too thin....the cheese will spurt out where it can...don't touch the meat...use the foil to roll the loaf using a spatula to encourage anything sticking to the foil...then when it is all sealed up (seam and ends) just roll it into the loaf pan off the foil...also make sure to drain this a couple of times during baking...i covered with foil til the last 20 mn then browned and it worked out nice....served with hot corn from this site and fried potatoes...num num

text:
The jelly roll thing for this was easy for me (had never tried it before) but may have been an accident lol Basically I picked up the end of the wax paper and started lifting, like I was gonna tip off the burger / fold it using the paper. Well, right as the first side started to roll over, I peeled the paper back and with one hand UNDER the edge of it, I just lifted the burger with my off hand (the one UNDER the wax paper), and peeled back the paper with  my main hand. Basically just rolling it, while peeling off the paper. I put the end of the paper on the cookie sheet and just rolled it right on. 

Other tweaks to list later: I added pickle juice to the meat. Added minced garlic. Replaced the reg salt & pepper with a combo of Lawry's and Celery salt, TINY amount of black pepper (for flavor, not heat) and Worcestershire.

Painted the loaf with drizzled olive oil And BBQ sauce. (non home made... Lazy :P).

After taking it out I moved it to ANOTHER cookie sheet due to the amount of grease. I had a POOL of it. So moving it over made me feel better then seeing it bathe in oil.

Tasted AMAZING and the pickle juice added a much more authentic burger taste. And Lawry's always brings out the taste of burger.

Gave it a 4 just because I could improve it still :P

text:
I am yet undecided with this recipe (I say this, but I've also made this more than once now, so maybe I like it more than I think I do?) First of all, the taste of cheddar and the flavor of red meat doesn't work with me. I've started using American cheese instead. Plus, to make things easier, I've used the suggestion of others to mold the meat into a bowl like shape, add the cheese, and then add the top half. This technique works, but I think it would taste better to make it as a jelly roll liked stated in the recipe. The cheese would be better distributed throughout. And perhaps because I haven't made it this way yet, the bake time is very off. I always have to bake it for so much longer, and it's still not as dry and cooked as I think meatloaf should be. I also don't put ketchup on the top out of preference.

text:
After reading the reviews, I thought the rolling might be difficult, but I found it to be a cinch.  I used the wax paper to help me roll it rather than touching the meatloaf with my hands.  It rolled right up - perfection.  When I went to get the cheese out of the frig, I noticed some string cheese, so I started my roll with those.  Then rather than pinching the ends, I sort of stuffed them shut with the hamburger.  It stayed together beautifully.  I did wait maybe 10 minutes before cutting it, and could have waited a few more but it didn't ooze too badly.  This was very good and is going in the rotation.  Thank you for sharing.

Although I had read all the rave reviews, I was still surprised this was so good. The meatloaf was very moist and flavorful and went wonderfully with roasted new potatoes. I would however, suggest that everyone take heed use and one of the alternate methods to "pinwheeling" the meat around the cheese as described in the recipe. I made this tonight for dinner.  IT'S AWESOME.  I am the only female in the house and my boys and hubby can get fussy.  The kids really enjoyed it so I know hubby will when he gets home from work.  I did make a few small changes and they worked out.  I didn't have ant bread crumbs, so I used 3/4 cup Dare Vinta Crackers crush up.  Instead of fresh onion, I used 1 package of Lipton Roasted Garlic Soup Mix.  I actually forgot to put in the pepper and only used one egg.  I used Kraft Tex Mex Shredded Cheese instead of just plain cheddar cheese.   I greased a loaf pan took half of the ground beef mixture on the bottom making a slight well all the way around.  Placed cheese on that layer, then covered the cheese layer with remaining ground beef and pressed it down firmly in order for all the sides to seal.  Covered it with foil and baked as indicated.  With this recipe you could do so many different things  Thank you for posting it.

text:
Excellent!  Even my 3 and 5 year old picky kids wanted seconds.  I made a few changes though combining this recipe and one I was given from a relative.  I mixed 1/2 cup ketchup, the eggs, seasoned bread crumbs, 1/4 cup minced onion, some onion salt and pepper together before adding the ground beef.  I sprayed foil with non-stick spray and flattened the meat out over it.  I spread 1/4-1/2 cup ketchup over the meat and I did not have shredded cheese so I used 4 slices of American and placed it over the meat.  I used the foil to help roll the meat up (rolling from the long side).  I then transferred the roll and the foil to a jelly roll pan (easier cleanup!).  After cooking for 50-60 minutes I used 3 more slices of cheese (cut diagonally) and layed them on top and put it back in the oven for 5-7 more minutes.  (The American cheese part was from the other recipe I had.  I would like to try the shredded cheese part but I really liked the American Cheese melted on top.  Gave a nice presentation and tasted great!)
***UPDATE: The second time I made this I tried it with the shredded cheese (2-3 cups) on the inside and it was much better than the sliced cheese.  I still used the slices on top for presentation purposes and this was a huge hit with everyone!

This on the regular rotation at our house. I use swiss cheese and mushrooms in the middle. Instead of doing all this extra work, just lay out a piece of parchment paper. Flatten your meat out leaving the edges a bit higher. Add your toppings in the middle and roll up, pulling paper back as you go. Pinch ends, put in meatloaf pan. I usually leave mine in for 90minutes at 350, then let sit for 15 or 20 so its not lava hot... Comes out perfect every time.

text:
For the simple ease of preparation, I halved the cheese and mixed it right into the meat. I always make meatloaf in a lightly greased 9x5 loaf pan as well. Seemed like it'd be too bland for our tastes, so I did add extra seasonings into the meat (garlic & onion powders, steak seasoning, worchestershire sauce and a handful of bacon bits and crushed french fried onions). My oven runs hot, so an hour was a little too long and produced a drier meatloaf than I prefer. Next time, 45 minutes will be sufficient. DH liked it better than my usual meatloaf (Brown Sugar Meatloaf, from AR). I brushed a mixture of ketchup, mustard and bbq sauce on top the last 1/2 hour of baking. Served with mashed potatoes and peas, it was a tasty Sunday night dinner.

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
I thought this was a fun twist to the typical meatloaf recipe, but gave it 4 stars since I had to come up a creative rolling technique and also thought the recipe could use a cheese sauce to top it since most of the cheese oozed out regardless that I sealed it well.  My brilliant rolling technique is to use an asian bamboo sushi wrap to roll it up.  It worked really well!  Be sure to cover the entire bamboo with syran wrap so you don't ruin your bamboo before rolling.  Spread the beefmix on the entire bamboo area, flat and even.  Spread the cheese on top and roll. Enclose the ends when finished rolling. To drain, I put a cooling rack over a serving platter and covered it to keep it warm before cutting.  Next time I will make this with mozzarella cheese, ground turkey, rosemary, and italian sausage & spices served with pasta and tomato sauce.  There are many ways this recipe can be modified, but the basic concept is a great idea! Thanks for sharing...

text:
This turned out really well, and it was very tasty. I followed the recipe as written, except I topped the meatloaf with ketchup before baking, which really was a finishing touch to the "cheeseburger" flavor. I didn't have any problems rolling this up, I used a sheet of waxed paper in a sided cookie sheet, and firmly pressed the meat mixture into the pan. I then added the cheese and it rolled up perfectly, and edges sealed nicely too! Be sure to let this rest for about 15-20 minutes while covered before cutting, or the cheese will all spill out. Sliced dill pickles is a nice little garnish for this, because it really does taste like acheeseburger! Thanks for sharing this recipe, I will use again (:

text:
Told the boyfriend that I was making meatloaf, and the epitome of picky eaters replied "I don't like meatloaf, it's gross". Something I hear nearly daily. I made this and topped it with a mixture of ketchup, mustard, and brown sugar, (and smothered my own in ketchup), and he asked for seconds! Juicy and delicious!

I give only 4 stars because I didn't like to cheese and the rolling, and I found the cook time to be inaccurate. The cheese ended up just kind of melting out and creating a layer of cheesy liquid in the bottom of the pan. I will not be adding the cheese part in the future.

As for cook time, one hour and it was still pink in the middle. Did 1.5 hours and it was perfect!

Delicious!  We loved it!  Will definitely make again.  I halved the recipe and had great results.  Here's a tip though, if you had problems rolling it up:  use the wax paper (or foil) to help you roll it.  Roll the paper forward, sealing any "breaks" in the loaf and pull the paper back each time until completely rolled. I am sure this was the intention for using wax paper.  It's really easy this way.  I love the little pinwheels I got when I cut into it.  Great for kids of all ages. (:

It is simple and easy, but as is, basic and really only tastes of cooked meat. Updated Aug 17 - nearly a year from original review:  I have made this several times now and it continues to be a hit.  I have mixed lean beef with ground turkey, ground sausage etc.  I have tried different cheeses, adding our favorite BBQ sauce, using a little bacon etc, etc.  I think the key is to not overwork it and to layit out on parchment and use that to "roll up".                                     
                               
              
Original review Oct 16:Delicious!  I followed basic instructions but sauteed mushroom and onions as part of the "filling" and reduced the cheese a bit.  I forgot to put anything on top and it was still wonderful.  Will make it again and try different flavor combinations.

I pressed the meat mixture out on a piece of baking parchment paper.  That paper helped me as I rolled it up and it was quite easy and stayed pretty firm.  Mine didn't slice as nicely as the photo but that is probably because we didn't let it cool for 15 minutes.  

Served with roasted vegetables and made a great dinner.

text:
My husband LOVES meatloaf...and the whole family is burned out on the brown sugar meatloaf recipe.  Great recipe, but needed a change.  This nailed it...delicious!!  A very picky 4 year old, a 5 year old, and my husband all wolfed it down.  And, I followed suit.  I didn't change anything (on purpose) but had added about 1 tbsp. of Worcestershire before I realized it actually did not call for it.  The only thing I did do different was place regular sliced bread in the bottom of the pan, then placed the meatloaf roll on foil that had small pricks to help drain the grease away from the loaf.  A suggestion from a review & it worked great.  After spreading the cheese, it rolled surprisingly easy, but only pulled away small lengths from the wax paper.  It seemed to roll tighter & had less holes to allow cheese to escape.  I saved 2 small meatball sized pieces of that mixture to help seal the ends.  Getting the 4 people in my house to all actually like a dish is rare.  Thank you Douglas!!  You just gave my family a new favorite meatloaf recipe (and to be honest, I thought I would never say that sentence in my life!)

text:
This is a good basic recipe, but there is plenty of room for jazzing it up.  Next time I will add sweet pepper, garlic, and a few other spices.  I didn't have any problem making the jelly roll.  Once I had the meat spread out on the wax paper and the cheese spread over the meat, I slipped one hand under the wax paper and used the paper to help me roll the meat.  As it began rolling, I peeled back the paper until the meat was all rolled up.  Then I pinched the outer edges closed and smoothed over the end of the roll so it wouldn't separate during baking.  Because some people mentioned having problems with too much grease, I placed my rolled up loaf on a piece of foil which I had spread over a baking rack.  I put the rack in my pan and used a fork to poke drain holes in the foil. All the fat drained into the pan and away from the loaf.  I used a meat thermometer and baked it to 155 degrees and then let it sit for 15 minutes. It reached 160 degrees as it sat.  After 15 minutes, it sliced perfectly.  My husband loved it.  I will definitely make it again.  Thanks for a great recipe!

text:
This is a wonderful take on traditional meatloaf. In order to achieve the jelly roll method I used 1 cup of bread crumbs instead of 3/4. I reduced the salt to 1 tsp. I also added 3 strips of raw bacon,cut into pieces along with 1 Tbls of Worstestershire sauce and a capful of liquid smoke to capture the taste of BBQ cheeseburgers. My family and friends love this. If you happen to have any leftovers, warm up the sliced meatloaf and put on hamburger buns.

great recipe. I am not a huge meatloaf fan but this is fantastic. Added green peppers for added flavor and topped with ketchup. Followed others recommendations and separated the meat mixture. Put the first half in the pan and then topped with cheese. Cover that w/ remaining meat-taking care to seal the edges so the cheese would not leak out from the two layers. Also cooked a broiler pan to allow the greese to drainm from the meatloaf as it cooks. Thanks for sharing the recipe!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Ya'll know I made some changes. First off I used turkey instead of beef. A full cup of bread crumbs. A whole white onion, minced. A cup of mushrooms, minced. Three eggs. No salt, no pepper. Only one cup of cheese maybe a cup and a quarter.

When working with the mixture, wash your hands and rebutter your hands every time you work with it. I've made this three times it gets better every time. Don't be afraid to and the salt and pepper to taste. I just can't take it.


First wisk the eggs. Then ad the onion and mushroom. Next bread crumbs and turkey. Mix that very thoroughly. Spray cooking oil on to a cookie sheet with a side wall of one inch. Push the mixture into the cookie sheet, try to make even. Then spread your cheese on the mixture. with the use of a spatula start to roll the mixture into a jell roll type roll. Rolling all the cheese inside. Do not try to pick it up. Simply slide the roll on the cookie sheet lengthwise to cook. An hour at 375-400. Cover for first 45 minutes with foil. Then uncover and finish cooking.

            Bon appetit!!!

I made this today, assembling it in the morning and refrigerating it until about an hour before I wanted to serve dinner. I had no problem with rolling the meatloaf because I put the meat mixture on a wax paper-lined countertop and used the paper to do the hard work. The cheese we had on hand was sharp cheddar cheese; I don't recommend it for this recipe for two reasons: it was just too sharp and it didn't melt appropriately. The meatloaf itself was better than many I've made in the past, but it wasn't as spectacular as I had hoped. I'm really hoping that the cold meatloaf sandwiches will be everything that I could possibly want tomorrow.

text:
Delicious and easy!  Wanted bacon cheeseburger so I added 1/2 cup of real bacon bits to the cheese and used saltines instead of bread.  Made it the night before and used the layering method of assembly in a loaf pan.   Refrigerate overnight and turn out onto a roasting pan before baking.  AB does this to eliminate the dreaded soggy bottom.  Topped with ketchup,  mustard and brown sugar glaze.   served with fried dill pickle chips,  French fries and a garden salad with 1000 island for the full burger effect.

text:
I've been making a very similar meatloaf (without the toppings) for about 40 years. It originally appeared in a little brochure put out by the Hunt's tomato people that included the lasagna recipe I always make. I've used ground beef and ground chicken as the meat for the meatloaf, with either grated cheddar or mozzarella cheeses for the filling, and baked the rolled-up loaf on a rimmed baking sheet. Both options are a hit but I've never thought of this meatloaf as a cheeseburger with typical cheeseburger toppings. I think leaving them to the various eaters is better, as different people like different toppings.

text:
To make rolling easier, lay long sheets of plastic wrap on the counter and spray with cooking spray.  Press the beef into a flat rectangle about 1/2 in. thick, or a little more, cover with cheese, and roll holding the plastic wrap as your guide (of course, discard the plastic when done).  If the meat is too thin the cheese will likely leak out once the beef starts cooking down.  Although that burnt cheese at the bottom of the pan is a treat in and of itself!  IMO, SHARP cheddar gives it the best flavor.

I made the recipe as written.  I used extra sharp cheddar which adds flavor to the beef.  To handle the grease I used lean ground beef and put slices of bread under the meatloaf.  They soak up the grease so that your meatloaf isn't greasy.  I rolled the meatloaf on non-stick (or sprayed) tinfoil.  Then slip the bread under and lift the loaf into the pan on the tinfoil to make for easy clean up.

text:
We loved this recipe.  I pretty much followed the recipe.  I did add more chopped onions (as we love them).  The rolling process was not hard at all.   I used parchment paper and was able to roll the meat by pulling the paper upwards and over so that the meat would basically roll on it's own.  Not hard at all like others had said in their reviews.   I put it on foil in a baking pan and added some ketchup across the top.  After it finished cooking, I did let it sit for at least 10 minutes (I would recommend longer because it was still oozing).  Of course, as the picture shows, we ate it with pickle chips.  Absolutely delicious and I will make it again.

text:
I am always looking for a new meatloaf recipe and thought I would give this a try.   I added a little ketchup & worcestershire sauce to the mix.   I did not have any problem rolling up the meatloaf as some people did.  I used my wax paper to roll the beef and it worked great.  That being said, I really don't think it needs to be rolled like a pinwheel.  Once it is cut, it is difficult to keep it together.  I think it would work better to just put a layer of meat down, fill with cheese, & top with a second layer.   In the end, we thought this was just ok with not a lot of flavor, so, I probably won't make again.

Scanned through all the recommendations on this recipe and made some changes. I used 95% lean ground beef , added 6 cloves of garlic to the mixture, used ground club crackers instead of bread crumbs. I took Amanda's tip to split the mixture in half and laid out one half in the baking dish, added my cheese mix of shredded 4 cheese Mexican and jalapeno jack.Then covered with the remaining meat mixture and tamped down the edges . Call it a Mexican cheeseburger meatloaf if you like but it was very tasty !!! May have to add sliced Jalapeno to the next one ... bon appetit !

text:
I really enjoyed this. I didn't have bread crumbs, so I toasted whole wheat bread in a 170 degree oven for 2 hours and then put in a food processor to make the crumbs. I used 93/7 beef and a silicon mat to roll the loaf. I sprayed the mat with cooking spray before patting out meat mixture onto the mat. I spread a thin layer of worcestershire on the meat before adding the cheese. Then, after rolling up the loaf, I added a thin layer of mustard and ketchup to the top. Baked 50 min on a cookie cooling rack placed in a jelly pan to a temperature of 155 (which raised to 159 upon sitting 5 minutes). Next time, I will try 85/15 beef. Good recipe. Thank you!

Tasted pretty decent; I am new to cooking, and my version of this looked absolutely ugly!

Pros: Very easy to make, and taste exactly how it is described (like a cheeseburger)

Cons: Gets very greasy, and breaks up too easy. I would suggest to the person that made this recipe to  give us a better idea of how THICK the rectangle of ground beef needs to be as opposed to what the dimensions should be. 

I ended up cutting this in to cubes with toothpicks so they could be dipped in to various sauces as opposed to slicing it up since it fell apart so easily. May make again, but not any time soon

I loved this! I tweaked it a bit more to what was on hand. I omitted the salt and pepper, and had to used dried minced onion. I also added about a tablespoon of rolled oats in addition to the bread crumbs. Instead of shredded cheddar, I shredded Buffalo Wing style cheese I bought in Wisconsin at Mouse Haus cheese house, and then topped the meat with "What a Jerk" caribbean style jerk sauce. Oh my, what flavor! M absolutely LOVED it! He wouldn't stop raving about it. I'll definitely be doing this again (with my additions as well), but I loved this recipe with the cheese incorporation; what inspiration to use as a springboard to a great meal. Thanks, Douglas!

I come here all the time, but I created a profile so I could review this!  As others have said, I also used lean beef so that it would cut down on the grease. I used a Colby-Jack blend of pre-shredded cheese as well. My onion was actually a frozen blend I had stuck in the freezer that I thought might sound good with this that has green and red pepper and celery with it. The rolling was a cinch, but I can see where it could get messy for some. It sealed nicely, so I didn't have any spillage. I also topped it with tomato sauce. It turned out great! My 17 month old liked it, so that says something! Kudos, and I love the roll! I don't know why I never did it before!

text:
I made this for a large group of children for a community center program in our town and it was a HUGE hit.  They gobbled every bit of it. Made with lean ground beef and paired with "oven" fries and fresh green beans, it was pretty healthy as well.  I followed previous advice and rather than do the jelly roll, pressed half the meat into the bottom of a 13x9 pan, then used 2 cups of cheese (3 seemed too much?).  I then pressed the remaining meat into a rectangle on wax paper and turned it on top of the cheese making sure to seal edges.  Because I was baking three pans at once, I still baked it for a little over an hour, but wonder if when baking one pan less time would be required.

My fiance ate this with no complaints.  He's not a meatloaf lover so I consider it a good effort!  I'm still looking for the "perfect" meatloaf but in the meantime this one will do nicely.  A suggestion, though ... he insisted that I use American cheese slices.  I'd recommend that anyone use SHREDDED cheese and NOT sliced because the slices kept sliding along on the meat and didn't get rolled up inside.  That was a big reason for a lot of the leakage.  I have a feeling that would not have happened if I'd used the shredded cheese like I planned.
